        <mi>q</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <mi>X</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <munder>
          <mo>&#x2211;<!-- ∑ --></mo>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>x</mi>
            <mo>&#x2208;<!-- ∈ --></mo>
            <mi>X</mi>
          </mrow>
        </munder>
        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
        <mi>p</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
        <mi>log</mi>
        <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mi>q</mi>
          <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
          <mi>x</mi>
          <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
        </mrow>
        <mspace width="thinmathspace" />
        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
        <mspace width="thinmathspace" />
        <munder>
          <mo>&#x2211;<!-- ∑ --></mo>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>x</mi>
            <mo>&#x2208;<!-- ∈ --></mo>
            <mi>X</mi>
          </mrow>
        </munder>
        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
        <mi>p</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
        <mi>log</mi>
        <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mi>p</mi>
          <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
          <mi>x</mi>
          <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
        </mrow>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <munder>
          <mo>&#x2211;<!-- ∑ --></mo>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>x</mi>
            <mo>&#x2208;<!-- ∈ --></mo>
            <mi>X</mi>
          </mrow>
        </munder>
        <mi>p</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
        <mi>log</mi>
        <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mfrac>
            <mrow>
              <mi>p</mi>
              <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
              <mi>x</mi>
              <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
            </mrow>
            <mrow>
              <mi>q</mi>
              <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
              <mi>x</mi>
              <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
            </mrow>
          </mfrac>
        </mrow>
        <mo>.</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle D_{\mathrm {KL} }(p(X)\|q(X))=\sum _{x\in X}-p(x)\log {q(x)}\,-\,\sum _{x\in X}-p(x)\log {p(x)}=\sum _{x\in X}p(x)\log {\frac {p(x)}{q(x)}}.}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4b6882199003743a8f6d6d0d4723b2bd2e496f98" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -3.171ex; width:80.622ex; height:7.009ex;" alt="{\displaystyle D_{\mathrm {KL} }(p(X)\|q(X))=\sum _{x\in X}-p(x)\log {q(x)}\,-\,\sum _{x\in X}-p(x)\log {p(x)}=\sum _{x\in X}p(x)\log {\frac {p(x)}{q(x)}}.}"></span></dd></dl>
<p>Although it is sometimes used as a 'distance metric', KL divergence is not a true <a href="/wiki/Metric_(mathematics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Metric (mathematics)">metric</a> since it is not symmetric and does not satisfy the <a href="/wiki/Triangle_inequality" title="Triangle inequality">triangle inequality</a> (making it a semi-quasimetric).
</p><p>Another interpretation of the KL divergence is the "unnecessary surprise" introduced by a prior from the truth: suppose a number <i><span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle X}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>X</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle X}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/68baa052181f707c662844a465bfeeb135e82bab" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.98ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle X}"></span></i> is about to be drawn randomly from a discrete set with probability distribution <span class="nowrap">&#8288;<span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle p(x)}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>p</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle p(x)}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8cb7afced134ef75572e5314a5d278c2d644f438" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; margin-left: -0.089ex; width:4.398ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle p(x)}"></span>&#8288;</span>. If Alice knows the true distribution <span class="nowrap">&#8288;<span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle p(x)}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>p</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle p(x)}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8cb7afced134ef75572e5314a5d278c2d644f438" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; margin-left: -0.089ex; width:4.398ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle p(x)}"></span>&#8288;</span>, while Bob believes (has a <a href="/wiki/Prior_probability" title="Prior probability">prior</a>) that the distribution is <span class="nowrap">&#8288;<span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle q(x)}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>q</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle q(x)}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c38bbafe34a043d284f19231b946a76c0a4b16b4" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:4.209ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle q(x)}"></span>&#8288;</span>, then Bob will be more <a href="/wiki/Information_content" title="Information content">surprised</a> than Alice, on average, upon seeing the value of <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle X}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>X</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle X}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/68baa052181f707c662844a465bfeeb135e82bab" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.98ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle X}"></span>. The KL divergence is the (objective) expected value of Bob's (subjective) <a href="/wiki/Information_content" title="Information content">surprisal</a> minus Alice's surprisal, measured in bits if the <i>log</i> is in base 2. In this way, the extent to which Bob's prior is "wrong" can be quantified in terms of how "unnecessarily surprised" it is expected to make him.
</p>

    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle X^{n}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/268db8293666fefd75cfb00513706171948edf09" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:3.215ex; height:2.343ex;" alt="{\displaystyle X^{n}}"></span> to <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle Y^{n}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msup>
          <mi>Y</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>n</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msup>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle Y^{n}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a6e8fe1b832e2088d10ef7c91d815a0d21aad4ca" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.171ex; width:3.119ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle Y^{n}}"></span>. The Directed information has many applications in problems where <a href="/wiki/Causality" title="Causality">causality</a> plays an important role such as <a href="/wiki/Channel_capacity" title="Channel capacity">capacity of channel</a> with feedback,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-massey&#95;51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-massey-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> capacity of discrete <a href="/wiki/Memoryless" class="mw-redirect" title="Memoryless">memoryless</a> networks with feedback,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sports_gambling" class="mw-redirect" title="Sports gambling">gambling</a> with causal side information,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Data_compression" title="Data compression">compression</a> with causal side information,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
<a href="/wiki/Real-time_control" class="mw-redirect" title="Real-time control">real-time control</a> communication settings,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and in statistical physics.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Other_quantities">Other quantities</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Information_theory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Other quantities"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Other important information theoretic quantities include the <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9nyi_entropy" title="Rényi entropy">Rényi entropy</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Tsallis_entropy" title="Tsallis entropy">Tsallis entropy</a> (generalizations of the concept of entropy), <a href="/wiki/Differential_entropy" title="Differential entropy">differential entropy</a> (a generalization of quantities of information to continuous distributions), and the <a href="/wiki/Conditional_mutual_information" title="Conditional mutual information">conditional mutual information</a>. Also, <a href="/wiki/Pragmatic_information" class="mw-redirect" title="Pragmatic information">pragmatic information</a> has been proposed as a measure of how much information has been used in making a decision.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Coding_theory">Coding theory</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Information_theory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Coding theory"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1305433154">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Coding_theory" title="Coding theory">Coding theory</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:CDSCRATCHES.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/CDSCRATCHES.jpg/250px-CDSCRATCHES.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="115" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5a/CDSCRATCHES.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="283" data-file-height="130" /></a><figcaption>A picture showing scratches on the readable surface of a CD-R. Music and data CDs are coded using error correcting codes and thus can still be read even if they have minor scratches using <a href="/wiki/Error_detection_and_correction" title="Error detection and correction">error detection and correction</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Coding theory is one of the most important and direct applications of information theory. It can be subdivided into source coding theory and channel coding theory. Using a statistical description for data, information theory quantifies the number of bits needed to describe the data, which is the information entropy of the source.
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Data_compression" title="Data compression">Data compression</a> (source coding): There are two formulations for the compression problem:
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Lossless_data_compression" class="mw-redirect" title="Lossless data compression">Lossless data compression</a>: the data must be reconstructed exactly;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lossy_data_compression" class="mw-redirect" title="Lossy data compression">Lossy data compression</a>: allocates bits needed to reconstruct the data, within a specified fidelity level measured by a distortion function. This subset of information theory is called <i><a href="/wiki/Rate%E2%80%93distortion_theory" title="Rate–distortion theory">rate–distortion theory</a></i>.</li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Error-correcting_code" class="mw-redirect" title="Error-correcting code">Error-correcting codes</a> (channel coding): While data compression removes as much redundancy as possible, an error-correcting code adds just the right kind of redundancy (i.e., error correction) needed to transmit the data efficiently and faithfully across a noisy channel.</li></ul>
<p>This division of coding theory into compression and transmission is justified by the information transmission theorems, or source–channel separation theorems that justify the use of bits as the universal currency for information in many contexts. However, these theorems only hold in the situation where one transmitting user wishes to communicate to one receiving user. In scenarios with more than one transmitter (the multiple-access channel), more than one receiver (the <a href="/wiki/Broadcast_channel" class="mw-redirect" title="Broadcast channel">broadcast channel</a>) or intermediary "helpers" (the <a href="/wiki/Relay_channel" title="Relay channel">relay channel</a>), or more general <a href="/wiki/Computer_network" title="Computer network">networks</a>, compression followed by transmission may no longer be optimal.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Source_theory">Source theory</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Information_theory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Source theory"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Any process that generates successive messages can be considered a <em><a href="/wiki/Communication_source" title="Communication source">source</a></em> of information. A memoryless source is one in which each message is an <a href="/wiki/Independent_identically_distributed_random_variables" class="mw-redirect" title="Independent identically distributed random variables">independent identically distributed random variable</a>, whereas the properties of <a href="/wiki/Ergodic_theory" title="Ergodic theory">ergodicity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stationary_process" title="Stationary process">stationarity</a> impose less restrictive constraints. All such sources are <a href="/wiki/Stochastic_process" title="Stochastic process">stochastic</a>. These terms are well studied in their own right outside information theory.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Rate">Rate</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Information_theory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Rate"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Information <i><a href="/wiki/Entropy_rate" title="Entropy rate">rate</a></i> is the average entropy per symbol. For memoryless sources, this is merely the entropy of each symbol, while, in the case of a stationary stochastic process, it is:

<p>that is, the limit of the joint entropy per symbol. For stationary sources, these two expressions give the same result.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>

<p>It is common in information theory to speak of the "rate" or "entropy" of a language. This is appropriate, for example, when the source of information is English prose. The rate of a source of information is related to its redundancy and how well it can be compressed, the subject of <em>source coding</em>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Channel_capacity">Channel capacity</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Information_theory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Channel capacity"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Channel_capacity" title="Channel capacity">Channel capacity</a></div>
<p>Communications over a channel is the primary motivation of information theory. However, channels often fail to produce exact reconstruction of a signal; noise, periods of silence, and other forms of signal corruption often degrade quality.
</p><p>Consider the communications process over a discrete channel. A simple model of the process is shown below:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {\xrightarrow[{\text{Message}}]{W}}{\begin{array}{|c| }\hline {\text{Encoder}}\\f_{n}\\\hline \end{array}}{\xrightarrow[{\mathrm {Encoded \atop sequence} }]{X^{n}}}{\begin{array}{|c| }\hline {\text{Channel}}\\p(y|x)\\\hline \end{array}}{\xrightarrow[{\mathrm {Received \atop sequence} }]{Y^{n}}}{\begin{array}{|c| }\hline {\text{Decoder}}\\g_{n}\\\hline \end{array}}{\xrightarrow[{\mathrm {Estimated \atop message} }]{\hat {W}}}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <munderover>
            <mo>&#x2192;</mo>
            <mpadded width="+0.611em" lspace="0.278em" voffset="-.24em">
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mtext>Message</mtext>
              </mrow>
            </mpadded>
            <mpadded width="+0.611em" lspace="0.278em" voffset=".15em">
              <mi>W</mi>
            </mpadded>
          </munderover>
        </mrow>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mtable rowspacing="4pt" columnspacing="1em" columnlines="" frame="solid">
            <mtr>
              <mtd>
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mtext>Encoder</mtext>
                </mrow>
              </mtd>
            </mtr>
            <mtr>
              <mtd>
                <msub>
                  <mi>f</mi>
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                    <mi>n</mi>
                  </mrow>
                </msub>
              </mtd>
            </mtr>
          </mtable>
        </mrow>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

<p>Here <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle X}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>X</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle X}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/68baa052181f707c662844a465bfeeb135e82bab" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.98ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle X}"></span> represents the space of messages transmitted, and <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\textstyle Y}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="false" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>Y</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\textstyle Y}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6222becc4f0c5effa012e5335b170575fdbbaad3" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.171ex; width:1.773ex; height:2.009ex;" alt="{\textstyle Y}"></span> the space of messages received during a unit time over our channel. Let <span class="texhtml"><i>p</i>(<i>y</i>&#124;<i>x</i>)</span> be the <a href="/wiki/Conditional_probability" title="Conditional probability">conditional probability</a> distribution function of <i><span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\textstyle Y}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="false" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>Y</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\textstyle Y}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6222becc4f0c5effa012e5335b170575fdbbaad3" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.171ex; width:1.773ex; height:2.009ex;" alt="{\textstyle Y}"></span></i> given <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle X}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>X</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle X}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/68baa052181f707c662844a465bfeeb135e82bab" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.98ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle X}"></span>. We will consider <span class="texhtml"><i>p</i>(<i>y</i>&#124;<i>x</i>)</span> to be an inherent fixed property of our communications channel (representing the nature of the <i><a href="/wiki/Signal_noise" class="mw-redirect" title="Signal noise">noise</a></i> of our channel). Then the joint distribution of <i><span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle X}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>X</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle X}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/68baa052181f707c662844a465bfeeb135e82bab" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.98ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle X}"></span></i> and <i><span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" alttext="{\textstyle Y}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="false" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>Y</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\textstyle Y}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6222becc4f0c5effa012e5335b170575fdbbaad3" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.171ex; width:1.773ex; height:2.009ex;" alt="{\textstyle Y}"></span></i> is completely determined by our channel and by our choice of <span class="texhtml"><i>f</i>(<i>x</i>)</span>, the marginal distribution of messages we choose to send over the channel. Under these constraints, we would like to maximize the rate of information, or the <i><a href="/wiki/Signal_(electrical_engineering)" class="mw-redirect" title="Signal (electrical engineering)">signal</a></i>, we can communicate over the channel. The appropriate measure for this is the mutual information, and this maximum mutual information is called the <em>channel capacity</em> and is given by:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle C=\max _{f}I(X;Y).\!}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>C</mi>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <munder>
          <mo movablelimits="true" form="prefix">max</mo>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>f</mi>
          </mrow>
        </munder>
        <mi>I</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <mi>X</mi>
        <mo>;</mo>
        <mi>Y</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
        <mo>.</mo>
        <mspace width="negativethinmathspace" />
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle C=\max _{f}I(X;Y).\!}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6d6698ae5326003e7530add14e24f875f834fb68" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; margin-right: -0.204ex; width:17.809ex; height:4.343ex;" alt="{\displaystyle C=\max _{f}I(X;Y).\!}"></span></dd></dl>
<p>This capacity has the following property related to communicating at information rate <i>R</i> (where <i>R</i> is usually bits per symbol). For any information rate <i>R</i> &lt; <i>C</i> and coding error <i>ε</i> &gt; 0, for large enough <i>N</i>, there exists a code of length <i>N</i> and rate ≥ R and a decoding algorithm, such that the maximal probability of block error is ≤ <i>ε</i>; that is, it is always possible to transmit with arbitrarily small block error. In addition, for any rate <i>R</i> &gt; <i>C</i>, it is impossible to transmit with arbitrarily small block error.
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Channel_code" class="mw-redirect" title="Channel code">Channel coding</a></i> is concerned with finding such nearly optimal codes that can be used to transmit data over a noisy channel with a small coding error at a rate near the channel capacity.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Capacity_of_particular_channel_models">Capacity of particular channel models</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Information_theory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Capacity of particular channel models"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li>A continuous-time analog communications channel subject to <a href="/wiki/Gaussian_noise" title="Gaussian noise">Gaussian noise</a>—see <a href="/wiki/Shannon%E2%80%93Hartley_theorem" title="Shannon–Hartley theorem">Shannon–Hartley theorem</a>.</li>
<li>A <a href="/wiki/Binary_symmetric_channel" title="Binary symmetric channel">binary symmetric channel</a> (BSC) with crossover probability <i>p</i> is a binary input, binary output channel that flips the input bit with probability <i>p</i>. The BSC has a capacity of <span class="texhtml">1 &#8722; <i>H</i><sub>b</sub>(<i>p</i>)</span> bits per channel use, where <span class="texhtml"><i>H</i><sub>b</sub></span> is the binary entropy function to the base-2 logarithm:</li></ul>
<dl><dd><dl><dd><span class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Binary_symmetric_channel.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Binary_symmetric_channel.svg/250px-Binary_symmetric_channel.svg.png" decoding="async" width="156" height="167" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Binary_symmetric_channel.svg/330px-Binary_symmetric_channel.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="156" data-file-height="167" /></a></span></dd></dl></dd></dl>
<ul><li>A <a href="/wiki/Binary_erasure_channel" title="Binary erasure channel">binary erasure channel</a> (BEC) with erasure probability <i>p</i> is a binary input, ternary output channel. The possible channel outputs are 0, 1, and a third symbol 'e' called an erasure. The erasure represents complete loss of information about an input bit. The capacity of the BEC is <span class="nowrap">1 &#8722; <i>p</i></span> bits per channel use.</li></ul>
<dl><dd><dl><dd><span class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Binary_erasure_channel.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Binary_erasure_channel.svg/250px-Binary_erasure_channel.svg.png" decoding="async" width="156" height="167" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Binary_erasure_channel.svg/330px-Binary_erasure_channel.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="156" data-file-height="167" /></a></span></dd></dl></dd></dl>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Channels_with_memory_and_directed_information">Channels with memory and directed information</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Information_theory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Channels with memory and directed information"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>

It is often more comfortable to use the notation <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle x^{i}=(x_{i},x_{i-1},x_{i-2},...,x_{1})}">

In such a case the capacity is given by the <a href="/wiki/Mutual_information" title="Mutual information">mutual information</a> rate when there is no feedback available and the <a href="/wiki/Directed_information" title="Directed information">Directed information</a> rate in the case that either there is feedback or not<sup id="cite&#95;ref-massey&#95;51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-massey-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> (if there is no feedback the directed information equals the mutual information).
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Fungible_information">Fungible information</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Information_theory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Fungible information"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><b>Fungible information</b> is the <a href="/wiki/Information" title="Information">information</a> for which the means of <a href="/wiki/Encoding" class="mw-redirect" title="Encoding">encoding</a> is not important.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Classical information theorists and computer scientists are mainly concerned with information of this sort. It is sometimes referred as speakable information.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Applications_to_other_fields">Applications to other fields</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Information_theory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Applications to other fields"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Network_Physiology">Network Physiology</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Information_theory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Network Physiology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Information theory concepts, methods and approaches have broad applications in Network Physiology<sup id="cite&#95;ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>, a field which provides a quantitative framework, based on adaptive networks of dynamical systems, to investigate how physiological systems exchange, process, and integrate information as a network to (i) coordinate their functions across levels and scales (from sub-cellular to organs and organism level) and (ii) generate distinct physiological states in health and disease. Through measures such as mutual information, transfer entropy, and co-information, information theory enables the detection of coupling strength, directionality, synergy/redundancy and higher-order interactions among physiological systems and sub-systems, revealing how network cross-communication and regulation occur within the organism. Applications of information-theoretic approaches span from analyzing information transfer between brain and body networks during various states<sup id="cite&#95;ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>; cardio-respiratory interactions<sup id="cite&#95;ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>; cardio-muscular interactions<sup id="cite&#95;ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>; cortico-muscular interactions<sup id="cite&#95;ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>; brain wave interactions and brain functional networks<sup id="cite&#95;ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>; Network Physiology in extreme environments<sup id="cite&#95;ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Intelligence_uses_and_secrecy_applications">Intelligence uses and secrecy applications</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Information_theory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Intelligence uses and secrecy applications"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1305433154" /><table class="box-Unreferenced&#95;section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="icon" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/60px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/120px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></span></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a href="/wiki/Special:EditPage/Information_theory" title="Special:EditPage/Information theory">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">April 2024</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Information theoretic concepts apply to cryptography and cryptanalysis. Turing's information unit, the <a href="/wiki/Ban_(unit)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ban (unit)">ban</a>, was used in the <a href="/wiki/Ultra_(cryptography)" title="Ultra (cryptography)">Ultra</a> project, breaking the German <a href="/wiki/Enigma_machine" title="Enigma machine">Enigma machine</a> code and hastening the <a href="/wiki/Victory_in_Europe_Day" title="Victory in Europe Day">end of World War II in Europe</a>. Shannon himself defined an important concept now called the <a href="/wiki/Unicity_distance" title="Unicity distance">unicity distance</a>. Based on the redundancy of the <a href="/wiki/Plaintext" title="Plaintext">plaintext</a>, it attempts to give a minimum amount of <a href="/wiki/Ciphertext" title="Ciphertext">ciphertext</a> necessary to ensure unique decipherability.
</p><p>Information theory leads us to believe it is much more difficult to keep secrets than it might first appear. A <a href="/wiki/Brute_force_attack" class="mw-redirect" title="Brute force attack">brute force attack</a> can break systems based on <a href="/wiki/Public-key_cryptography" title="Public-key cryptography">asymmetric key algorithms</a> or on most commonly used methods of <a href="/wiki/Symmetric-key_algorithm" title="Symmetric-key algorithm">symmetric key algorithms</a> (sometimes called secret key algorithms), such as <a href="/wiki/Block_cipher" title="Block cipher">block ciphers</a>. The security of all such methods comes from the assumption that no known attack can break them in a practical amount of time.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Information_theoretic_security" class="mw-redirect" title="Information theoretic security">Information theoretic security</a> refers to methods such as the <a href="/wiki/One-time_pad" title="One-time pad">one-time pad</a> that are not vulnerable to such brute force attacks. In such cases, the positive conditional mutual information between the plaintext and ciphertext (conditioned on the <a href="/wiki/Key_(cryptography)" title="Key (cryptography)">key</a>) can ensure proper transmission, while the unconditional mutual information between the plaintext and ciphertext remains zero, resulting in absolutely secure communications. In other words, an eavesdropper would not be able to improve his or her guess of the plaintext by gaining knowledge of the ciphertext but not of the key. However, as in any other cryptographic system, care must be used to correctly apply even information-theoretically secure methods; the <a href="/wiki/Venona_project" title="Venona project">Venona project</a> was able to crack the one-time pads of the Soviet Union due to their improper reuse of key material.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Pseudorandom_number_generation">Pseudorandom number generation</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Information_theory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Pseudorandom number generation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1305433154" /><table class="box-Unreferenced&#95;section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="icon" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/60px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/120px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></span></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a href="/wiki/Special:EditPage/Information_theory" title="Special:EditPage/Information theory">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">April 2024</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><a href="/wiki/Pseudorandom_number_generator" title="Pseudorandom number generator">Pseudorandom number generators</a> are widely available in computer language libraries and application programs. They are, almost universally, unsuited to cryptographic use as they do not evade the deterministic nature of modern computer equipment and software. A class of improved random number generators is termed <a href="/wiki/Cryptographically_secure_pseudorandom_number_generator" title="Cryptographically secure pseudorandom number generator">cryptographically secure pseudorandom number generators</a>, but even they require <a href="/wiki/Random_seed" title="Random seed">random seeds</a> external to the software to work as intended. These can be obtained via <a href="/wiki/Extractor_(mathematics)" title="Extractor (mathematics)">extractors</a>, if done carefully. The measure of sufficient randomness in extractors is <a href="/wiki/Min-entropy" title="Min-entropy">min-entropy</a>, a value related to Shannon entropy through <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9nyi_entropy" title="Rényi entropy">Rényi entropy</a>; Rényi entropy is also used in evaluating randomness in cryptographic systems. Although related, the distinctions among these measures mean that a random variable with high Shannon entropy is not necessarily satisfactory for use in an extractor and so for cryptography uses.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Seismic_exploration">Seismic exploration</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Information_theory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Seismic exploration"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>One early commercial application of information theory was in the field of seismic oil exploration. Work in this field made it possible to strip off and separate the unwanted noise from the desired seismic signal. Information theory and <a href="/wiki/Digital_signal_processing" title="Digital signal processing">digital signal processing</a> offer a major improvement of resolution and image clarity over previous analog methods.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Semiotics">Semiotics</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Information_theory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Semiotics"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Semiotics" title="Semiotics">Semioticians</a> <a href="/w/index.php?title=Doede_Nauta&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Doede Nauta (page does not exist)">Doede Nauta</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;&#91;<a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doede_Nauta" class="extiw" title="nl:Doede Nauta">nl</a>&#93;</span> and <a href="/wiki/Winfried_N%C3%B6th" title="Winfried Nöth">Winfried Nöth</a> both considered <a href="/wiki/Charles_Sanders_Peirce" title="Charles Sanders Peirce">Charles Sanders Peirce</a> as having created a theory of information in his works on semiotics.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Nauta&#95;1972&#95;82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nauta_1972-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 171">&#58;&#8202;171&#8202;</span></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Nöth&#95;2012&#95;83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nöth_2012-83"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 137">&#58;&#8202;137&#8202;</span></sup> Nauta defined semiotic information theory as the study of "<i>the internal processes of coding, filtering, and information processing.</i>"<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Nauta&#95;1972&#95;82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nauta_1972-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 91">&#58;&#8202;91&#8202;</span></sup>
</p><p>Concepts from information theory such as redundancy and code control have been used by semioticians such as <a href="/wiki/Umberto_Eco" title="Umberto Eco">Umberto Eco</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ferruccio_Rossi-Landi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ferruccio Rossi-Landi (page does not exist)">Ferruccio Rossi-Landi</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;&#91;<a href="https://it.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ferruccio_Rossi-Landi" class="extiw" title="it:Ferruccio Rossi-Landi">it</a>&#93;</span> to explain ideology as a form of message transmission whereby a dominant social class emits its message by using signs that exhibit a high degree of redundancy such that only one message is decoded among a selection of competing ones.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Integrated_process_organization_of_neural_information">Integrated process organization of neural information</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Information_theory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Integrated process organization of neural information"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Quantitative information theoretic methods have been applied in <a href="/wiki/Cognitive_science" title="Cognitive science">cognitive science</a> to analyze the integrated process organization of neural information in the context of the <a href="/wiki/Binding_problem" title="Binding problem">binding problem</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cognitive_neuroscience" title="Cognitive neuroscience">cognitive neuroscience</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In this context, either an information-theoretical measure, such as <em>functional clusters</em> (<a href="/wiki/Gerald_Edelman" title="Gerald Edelman">Gerald Edelman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Giulio_Tononi" title="Giulio Tononi">Giulio Tononi</a>'s functional clustering model and dynamic core hypothesis (DCH)<sup id="cite&#95;ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>) or <em>effective information</em> (Tononi's <a href="/wiki/Integrated_information_theory" title="Integrated information theory">integrated information theory</a> (IIT) of consciousness<sup id="cite&#95;ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>89<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>), is defined (on the basis of a reentrant process organization, i.e. the synchronization of neurophysiological activity between groups of neuronal populations), or the measure of the minimization of free energy on the basis of statistical methods (<a href="/wiki/Karl_J._Friston" title="Karl J. Friston">Karl J. Friston</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Free_energy_principle" title="Free energy principle">free energy principle</a> (FEP), an information-theoretical measure which states that every adaptive change in a self-organized system leads to a minimization of free energy, and the <a href="/wiki/Bayesian_brain" class="mw-redirect" title="Bayesian brain">Bayesian brain</a> hypothesis<sup id="cite&#95;ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>91<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>92<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>93<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>94<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>).
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Miscellaneous_applications">Miscellaneous applications</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Information_theory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Miscellaneous applications"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Information theory also has applications in the <a href="/wiki/Search_for_extraterrestrial_intelligence" title="Search for extraterrestrial intelligence">search for extraterrestrial intelligence</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>95<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Black_hole_information_paradox" title="Black hole information paradox">black holes</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>96<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bioinformatics" title="Bioinformatics">bioinformatics</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>97<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Gambling_and_information_theory" title="Gambling and information theory">gambling</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>98<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>99<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><br />
</p>
